The Rule of Adding Newly Acquired Wealth (al-Mustafād) to Nisab in Zakat
Ruling on adding new wealth and intra-Hanafi dispute on sale proceeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi rule for adding newly acquired wealth to existing nisab, apply the condition of same type (jins), and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sale proceeds of livestock.

Core Idea
New wealth of the same type joins the existing nisab, but sale proceeds of livestock after zakat do not join cash according to Abu Hanifah.

In zakat, the annual cycle (hawl) is central. But what happens when you acquire new wealth mid-year? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: if the new wealth is of the same type as your existing nisab, you add it and pay zakat on the total at the end of the original year. But a specific case concerning the sale of zakat-paid livestock creates a dispute between Abu Hanifah and his two chief disciples. This lesson unpacks that dispute and identifies the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule of al-ḍamm
Identify the principle that newly acquired wealth of the same type is added to existing nisab, and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the original year.
This applies regardless of how the wealth was acquired (inheritance, gift, etc.).
2
Identify the condition: same type (jins)
Note that the rule only applies if the new wealth is of the same type as the existing nisab (e.g., cash with cash, sheep with sheep). Different types are not added.
Example: sheep are not added to camels.
3
Present the specific case
Consider a person who had nisab of grazing livestock (sāʾimah), completed the year and paid zakat, then sold the animals for dirhams, while also owning a nisab of dirhams for half a year.
4
Contrast the views of Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifah rules that the sale proceeds do not join the existing dirhams but start a new year. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that they are added to the existing dirhams and zakat is paid together.
The difference hinges on whether the haw of the original livestock transfers to the cash after sale.
5
Determine the muftā bihī and thamarah al-khilāf
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifah. Practically, this means zakat on the sale proceeds is delayed by a year compared to the disciples' view.
This affects the timing and amount of zakat due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن كان له نصاب، فاستفاد في أثناء الحول مالاً من جنسه : ضمه إلى ماله، وزكّاه به). سواء كان المستفاد من نمائه، أو لا، وبأي وجه استفاده: ضمه، سواء كان بميراث، أو هبة، أو غير ذلك. وشرط كونه من جنسه: إذ لو كان من غير جنسه من كل وجه، كالغنم مع الإبل : فإنه لا يُضَم. ثم لو كان معه نصاب من السائمة حال عليها الحول، فزكاها، باعها بدراهم، ومعه نصاب من الدراهم قد مضى عليه نصف الحول: فعند أبي حنيفة لا يَضُمُّ إليه ثمن السائمة، بل يستأنف له حولاً جديداً. وعندهما يضمه، ويزكيهما جميعاً.
He said: (And whoever has a nisab, and then acquires during the year wealth of the same type, he adds it to his wealth and pays zakat on it together). Whether the acquired wealth is from its growth or not, and by any means he acquired it: he adds it, whether by inheritance, gift, or otherwise. The condition is that it be of the same type; if it is entirely of a different type, like sheep with camels, then it is not added. Then, if he had a nisab of livestock (sāʾimah) on which the year had passed, he paid zakat on it, then sold it for dirhams, and he also has a nisab of dirhams on which half the year has passed: according to Abū Ḥanīfah, he does not add the price of the livestock to it, but starts a new year for it. According to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), he adds it and pays zakat on both together.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage deals with the rule of adding newly acquired wealth (mustafād) to existing nisab during the zakat year. The base text states that if a person already possesses a nisab and acquires additional wealth of the same type (jins) during the year, he must add it to his existing wealth and pay zakat on the total when the year completes for the original nisab. The commentator clarifies that this applies whether the acquisition is from natural growth (e.g., offspring) or not, and by any means such as inheritance or gift. However, it only applies if the new wealth is of the same type as the existing nisab (e.g., cash with cash, livestock with the same species). The passage then presents a specific case illustrating a dispute between Abū Ḥanīfah and the two disciples (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī). If someone had a nisab of grazing livestock, completed a year and paid zakat, then sold the animals for cash (dirhams) while already owning a nisab of dirhams that had half a year remaining: Abū Ḥanīfah says the cash from the sale does not join the existing dirhams; instead, a new year starts for the sale proceeds. The two disciples say the sale proceeds are added to the existing dirhams, and zakat is paid on both at the end of the year of the existing dirhams. The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school is that of Abū Ḥanīfah in this case, as per later authorities.

Key Terms
المستفاد (al-mustafād): Wealth acquired during the zakat year, whether by growth, inheritance, gift, etc.
الضم (al-ḍamm): Adding newly acquired wealth to existing nisab for zakat calculation.
السائمة (al-sāʾimah): Grazing livestock that are left to pasture freely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Ḥanīfah, if a person sells his zakat-paid livestock for dirhams while already having a nisab of dirhams for half a year, what should he do?
A) Add the sale proceeds to the existing dirhams and pay zakat together
B) Start a new year for the sale proceeds
C) Pay zakat only on the existing dirhams
D) Give zakat on the livestock again

Key Takeaway
When adding newly acquired wealth to nisab, same type is required; but sale proceeds of livestock after zakat do not join existing cash – they start a new year per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Zakat Collector Must Avoid Taking Nursing, Fattened, Stud, and Pregnant Animals
Lists animals the zakat collector must avoid taking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four types of animals the zakat collector must avoid taking and explain the evidence from the action of ʿUmar (RA).

Core Idea
Zakat collector must not take nursing, fattened, stud, or pregnant animals to preserve the owner's livelihood.

This passage lists specific animals that the zakat collector should not take when collecting livestock zakat. The collector is also reminded that blind, old, and young animals are counted in the nisab but are not taken. The ruling is based on the instruction of ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb (RA) to his collector, showing the school's reliance on the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed animals
The text names four types of animals the collector must avoid: rabāʾ (nursing females), akūlah (fattened for slaughter), faḥl (stud male), and ḥāmil (pregnant female).
These are animals essential for the owner's livelihood or for reproduction.
2
Note the counting rule
The text adds that blind, old, and small animals are counted in the nisab but not taken. They are considered part of the wealth but are not collected.
This prevents hardship on the owner.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the athar of ʿUmar (RA): 'Count for them the lamb... but do not take it.' This is a Companion practice considered a proof in Hanafi usul.
The athar is quoted in the text.
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The command to count but not take implies that animals with particular utility (young, nursing, working, etc.) should not be collected. By analogy, other beneficial animals are also exempt.
The reasoning is based on preventing harm to the owner.
5
Confirm the ruling
The Hanafi school considers it wajib for the collector to avoid these animals; taking them is makruh tahrimi. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is from the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يأخذ الرباء، وهي التي تُربِّي ولدَها، ولا الأكولة، وهي التي تُسمن للأكل، ولا الفحل، ولا الحامل). ويُحسب عليه في سائمته العمياء والعجفاء والصغيرة، ولا يأخذ منها شيئاً؛ «القول عمر رضي الله عنه لساعيه : عُدَّ عليهم السخلة ولو أتاك بها الراعي على كفه، ولا تأخذها»(۱).
He said: (And he should not take the rabāʾ – which is the one raising her young – nor the akūlah – which is the one fattened for eating – nor the stallion, nor the pregnant one). And counted for him (the owner) in his grazing livestock are the blind, the old, and the small, but he does not take anything from them; [based on] the statement of ʿUmar (may Allah be pleased with him) to his collector: 'Count for them the lamb even if the shepherd brings it on his palm, but do not take it.'
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage gives further guidelines for the zakat collector on which specific animals to avoid taking. The base text mentions four types: (1) rabāʾ – an animal that is nursing its young, (2) akūlah – an animal being fattened for consumption, (3) the stallion (faḥl) used for breeding, and (4) the pregnant one (ḥāmil). The commentator adds that while these are not taken, certain other animals are counted in the nisab but not collected: the blind, the old (ʿajfāʾ), and the young (ṣaghīrah). The proof is the action of ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb (RA) who instructed his collector to count even a lamb for the owner but not to take it. This is an athar (saying of a Companion) used as evidence in the Hanafi school. The wisdom is to preserve the owner's source of livelihood and not to burden them with essential animals.

Key Terms
الرباء (al-rabāʾ): A female animal that is nursing its offspring.
الأكولة (al-akūlah): An animal fattened for slaughter and eating.
الفحل (al-faḥl): A stud male animal used for breeding.
السخلة (al-sakhlah): A young lamb or kid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) al-rabāʾ
B) al-akūlah
C) al-ʿajfāʾ
D) al-faḥl

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector must avoid taking animals that are nursing, fattened, stud, or pregnant, based on the practice of ʿUmar (RA).

Ruling on Appending Newly Acquired Same-Type Assets for Zakat
Ruling statement with proof from Umar's instruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of appending newly acquired same-type wealth to the existing nisab and state the exceptions and proof.

Core Idea
Newly acquired wealth of the same type is appended to the existing nisab; zakat is due on the total at year-end, even if acquired mid-year.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and its commentary establish a key principle in Hanafi zakat law: when a person already possesses a nisab and then acquires additional wealth of the same type during the zakat year, the new wealth is added to the existing nisab, and zakat is paid on the combined amount at the end of the year. The ruling applies regardless of the source of acquisition—inheritance, gift, or growth—provided the genus is the same. The text also clarifies which animals are not taken by the collector, though they are counted in the nisab, and provides a hadith from Umar as proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the acquisition of additional wealth of the same type during the zakat year. The ruling: it must be appended to the existing nisab, and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the year.
The ruling is wajib based on the hadith and qiyas.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Umar (attributed to him) instructing his collector: 'Count for them the lamb even if the shepherd brings it to you on his palm, but do not take it.' This indicates that even the smallest newborn is counted in the nisab.
The hadith is ahad, with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'count' (ʿudda) implies inclusion of the newly acquired animal in the nisab calculation. The prohibition 'do not take' indicates that the collector should not take it as zakat at the moment but should count it for the total.
This supports appending mid-year acquisitions.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that newly acquired wealth of a different genus or even same genus starts its own zakat year unless it is from the growth of the original nisab. Hanafis append regardless of source as long as the genus is the same.
The practical difference: a smaller zakat amount for Shafi'is vs. larger for Hanafis.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) and is supported by the hadith of Umar and the principle of public interest (maslaha) in unifying the zakat year.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الخيل
ومن كان له نصاب، فاستفاد في أثناء الحول من جنسه : ضَمَّه إليه، وزكّاه به.
ولا يأخذ الرباء، وهي التي تُربِّي ولدَها، ولا الأكولة، وهي التي تُسمن للأكل، ولا الفحل، ولا الحامل.
ويحسب عليه في سائمته العمياء والعجفاء والصغيرة، ولا يأخذ منها شيئاً؛ «القول عمر رضي الله عنه لساعيه : عُدَّ عليهم السخلة ولو أتاك بها الراعي على كفه، ولا تأخذها»(۱).
* قوله: (ومن كان له نصاب، فاستفاد في أثناء الحول مالاً من جنسه : ضمه إلى ماله، وزكّاه به).
سواء كان المستفاد من نمائه، أو لا، وبأي وجه استفاده: ضمه، سواء كان بميراث، أو هبة، أو غير ذلك.
وشرط كونه من جنسه: إذ لو كان من غير جنسه من كل وجه،
كالغنم مع الإبل : فإنه لا يُضَم.
Chapter on Zakat of Horses. Whoever has a nisab and acquires during the year from its type: he adds it to his wealth and pays zakat on it. He does not take the nursing mother, and it is the one that raises its young; nor the fattened one, which is fattened for eating; nor the stud; nor the pregnant. He is counted for his grazing animals the blind, the thin, and the small, and he does not take anything from them. The saying of Umar [may Allah be pleased with him] to his collector: 'Count for them the lamb even if the shepherd brings it to you on his palm, but do not take it.' * His statement: (Whoever has a nisab and acquires during the year wealth from its type: he adds it to his wealth and pays zakat on it). Whether the acquired is from its growth or not, and by whatever means he acquired it: he adds it, whether by inheritance, gift, or otherwise. The condition is that it be from its type: for if it is from a different type in every respect, like sheep with camels: then it is not added.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Mukhtasar al-Quduri followed by commentary from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira. It addresses the case where a person already possesses a nisab (minimum threshold for zakat) and, during the zakat year, acquires additional wealth of the same type (e.g., more sheep if one already has a nisab of sheep). The ruling: the newly acquired wealth is added to the existing nisab, and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the year, even if the new acquisition has not completed its own year. This is subject to the condition that the new wealth is of the same genus (jins). The commentary clarifies that it does not matter whether the acquisition comes from the growth of the original wealth or from an external source like inheritance or gift. The text then lists exceptions: certain animals are not taken by the collector (the nursing mother, the fattened for eating, the stud, the pregnant), though they are counted in the nisab. Blind, thin, and small animals are counted but not taken. The hadith from Umar supports counting even the smallest lamb but not taking it. The key condition is same genus; for example, sheep are not added to camels because they are different genera.

Key Terms
السائمة (al-sā'imah): Grazing livestock that subsist on pasture for most of the year.
الرباء (al-ribā'): The mother animal that raises its young, not taken as zakat but counted in nisab.
الأكولة (al-akūlah): The animal fattened for consumption, not taken as zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The 10 sheep are not subject to zakat until they complete a full year.
B) The 10 sheep are added to the existing nisab, and zakat is paid on all 50 at the end of the year.
C) The 10 sheep must be given as zakat immediately.
D) The 10 sheep are not added because they are a gift.

Key Takeaway
Newly acquired wealth of the same type as the existing nisab is appended for zakat calculation, and zakat is due on the combined total at the end of the zakat year.

Appending Sale Proceeds of Zakat Livestock to Cash Nisab: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Discusses ruling on adding price of sold zakat livestock to existing cash nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on appending the sale price of zakat livestock to an existing cash nisab, and identify the conditions that lead to consensus.

Core Idea
Sale price of zakat livestock is appended only if it does not reach a nisab alone; otherwise, Abu Hanifa starts a new year.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayrah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific zakat scenario: a person who already has a cash nisab in progress sells zakat livestock after paying zakat on them. Abu Hanifa rules that the sale price begins a new zakat year, while his two disciples append it to the existing cash nisab. Understanding this difference is key to correctly calculating zakat when multiple forms of wealth are involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputing parties
Note the precise setup: a person had a nisab of grazing livestock, completed a year, paid zakat, then sold them for dirhams. He also has a nisab of dirhams halfway through its zakat year. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and its trigger condition
Abu Hanifa says: do not append the price to the cash nisab; instead, start a new zakat year for the price from the date of sale. This applies when the sale price alone reaches a nisab.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling and its principle
The Sahibayn say: append the price to the existing cash nisab and pay zakat on both together at the end of the cash nisab's year.
4
List the consensus cases
When the sale price is less than a nisab, it is appended by consensus. Also appended by consensus: the price of tithed food, the price of a slave who paid fitr, livestock sold before its own zakat year, and livestock turned into fodder after zakat.
5
Determine the practical consequence of the khilaf
The practical result: following Abu Hanifa delays zakat on the sale price by up to a year compared to following the Sahibayn. This affects when zakat must be paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم
ولو كان معه نصاب من السائمة حال عليها الحول، فزكاها، باعها بدراهم، ومعه نصاب من الدراهم قد مضى عليه نصف الحول: فعند أبي حنيفة لا يَضُمُّ إليه ثمن السائمة، بل يستأنف له حولاً جديداً.
وعندهما يضمه، ويزكيهما جميعاً.
وهذا إذا كان ثمن السائمة يبلغ نصاباً بانفراده، أما إذا كان لا يبلغ نصاباً: ضمه، بالإجماع.
وأما ثمن الطعام المعشور، وثمن العبد الذي أدى صدقة فطره: فإنه يُضم، إجماعاً.
ولو باع الماشية قبل الحول بدراهم، أو بماشية: ضَمَّ الثمن إلى جنسه، بالإجماع، أي يضم الدراهم إلى الدراهم، والماشية إلى الماشية. وإن جعل الماشية بعد ما زكَّاها علوفةٌ، ثم باعها : ضم ثمنها، إجماعاً؛ لأنها خرجت عن حكم مال الزكاة، فلم تبق نصاباً.
Then: If he had a nisab of grazing animals, the year passed over it, he paid zakat on it, sold them for dirhams, and he had a nisab of dirhams half of which had passed: according to Abu Hanifa he does not append the price of the grazing animals to it, but rather starts a new year for it. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he appends it and pays zakat on both together. This is if the price of the grazing animals reaches a nisab by itself. If it does not reach a nisab: he appends it, by consensus. As for the price of the tithed food and the price of the slave who paid his charity of fitr: it is appended, by consensus. If he sold the livestock before the year for dirhams or for livestock: he appends the price to its type, by consensus; meaning he appends dirhams to dirhams, and livestock to livestock. And if he made the livestock after paying zakat on it fodder, then sold it: he appends its price, by consensus; because it left the ruling of zakat wealth, so it no longer remains a nisab.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage details an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the treatment of proceeds from the sale of zakat livestock when the seller already possesses a cash nisab (dirhams) that has not completed its year. The scenario: a person has a nisab of grazing livestock, completes a year, pays zakat on them, then sells them for dirhams. He also has a separate nisab of dirhams that is halfway through its zakat year. Abu Hanifa rules that the sale price is not appended to the existing cash nisab; instead, a new zakat year starts for the price from the date of sale. The two scholars (Sahibayn) rule that the price is appended to the existing cash nisab, and zakat is paid on both together at the end of the cash nisab's year. The text then notes exceptions: if the sale price does not reach a nisab by itself, there is consensus that it is appended. Similarly, the price of tithed food and the price of a slave who paid fitr are appended by consensus. Furthermore, if livestock is sold before the completion of its own zakat year, the price is appended to its type by consensus. If after paying zakat the livestock is made into fodder (thus leaving zakat eligibility) and then sold, the price is appended by consensus because the livestock is no longer zakatable wealth.

Key Terms
السائمة (al-sā'imah): Grazing livestock that qualify for zakat.
ضم (ḍamm): To append or add new wealth to an existing nisab for zakat calculation.

A) The price is appended to the dirhams and zakat is paid together.
B) A new zakat year starts for the price, separate from the dirhams.
C) The price is not subject to zakat at all.
D) The dirhams are appended to the price.

Key Takeaway
When the sale price of zakat livestock reaches a nisab, Abu Hanifa starts a new year; the Sahibayn append it to existing cash. If the price is less than a nisab, all agree to append.

Definition and Conditions of Sa'imah for Zakat on Livestock
Defines sa'imah and states conditions for zakat obligation on grazing animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sa'imah and state the conditions that trigger or remove zakat obligation on grazing livestock according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock is due only for sa'imah kept for milk/offspring; fed half the year or trade/transport use cancels it.

The term sa'imah refers to livestock that subsist on natural pasture for most of the year. However, not every grazing animal incurs zakat. The Hanafi school specifies that zakat is obligatory only when the animals are kept for their milk and offspring — not for trade or transport. Moreover, if the owner feeds them for half the year or more, they cease to be considered sa'imah. This lesson unpacks these conditions.

Guided Path
1
Define sa'imah
Identify the key condition: animals must rely on pasture for more than half the year. Occasional feeding does not negate sa'imah status if grazing is the majority.
'Most of the year' means > half the year.
2
Identify the purpose requirement
Zakat is only due if animals are kept for milk and offspring (productive purposes). Animals kept for trade or riding/carrying are exempt from livestock zakat.
Trade animals may be subject to trade zakat (zakat al-‘urūḍ).
3
Apply the feeding exception
If the owner feeds the animals for half the year or more, they are not considered sa'imah. If fed exactly half, the ruling is that they are not sa'imah.
The threshold is 6 months or more of feeding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والسائمة : هي التي تكتفي بالرعي في أكثر حولها). لأن أصحاب السوائم قد لا يجدون بداً من أن يعلفوا سوائمهم في بعض الأوقات، فجعل الأقل تابعاً للأكثر .
ثم هذا الذي ذكره من الإسامة في حق إيجاب زكاة السوائم: إنما أن لو كانت الإسامة للدَّرِّ ،والنسل، أما إذا كانت للتجارة)، أو يصح للحمل والركوب : فلا تجب فيها الزكاة أصلاً.
قوله: (فإن عَلَفَها نصف الحول، أو أكثر : فلا زكاة عليه فيها).
His statement: (The grazing animals are those that suffice on pasture for most of their year). Because owners of grazing animals may inevitably have to feed them in some periods, so the lesser is made subsidiary to the greater. Then this that he mentioned of grazing regarding the obligation of zakat on grazing animals: it is only if the grazing is for milk and offspring. As for if it is for trade, or if it is for carrying and riding: then no zakat is due on them at all. His statement: (If he fed them for half the year or more, then no zakat is due on him for them).
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'sa'imah' (grazing livestock) and clarifies the conditions under which zakat becomes obligatory on them. The definition: animals that rely on pasture for the majority of the year. The commentary explains that owners may need to feed them occasionally, but the majority rule applies: if they graze most of the year, they are considered sa'imah. However, even if animals are sa'imah, zakat is only due if the purpose of keeping them is for their milk and offspring (i.e., for breeding and production). If the animals are kept for trade (as merchandise) or for carrying and riding, no zakat is due on them as livestock zakat; trade goods are subject to a different zakat regime. The text also states that if the owner feeds the animals for half the year or more, they are not considered sa'imah and thus no zakat is due on them. This ruling establishes that zakat on livestock is contingent upon the mode of feeding and the intention of ownership.

Key Terms
السائمة (al-sā'imah): Grazing livestock that subsist on pasture for more than half the year.
الإسامة (al-isāmah): The condition of being grazing animals; the state of relying on pasture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Zakat on livestock is not automatic; it requires the animals to be sa'imah, kept for milk/offspring, and not fed half the year.

Definition of Sā'imah and Conditions for Zakat on Grazing Livestock
Definition and condition ruling for zakat on livestock

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sā'imah, identify the condition of grazing for most of the year, and apply the ruling when feeding equals or exceeds half the year.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock is only fard if they graze freely for more than half the year; otherwise, the condition is not met.

In Hanafi fiqh, zakat on livestock is not a blanket obligation. It depends on whether the animals are sā'imah—those that find their own food from natural pasture for the majority of the year. This lesson dissects that definition and the crucial feeding rule, including what happens when grazing and feeding are equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
What is the act being ruled upon? Zakat on livestock. It is an ibadah, a financial worship. Note that the core definition is 'sā'imah'.
2
Define sā'imah precisely
From the passage: 'as-sā'imah are those that suffice with pasture for most of their year.' Determine what 'most' means numerically: it must be more than half the year.
The opposite is 'alūfah'—fed by the owner.
3
Apply the feeding rule
If the owner feeds the animals for half the year or more, they are not sā'imah, so no zakat is due on them as livestock. The lesser period is subsidiary to the greater.
If grazing and feeding are equal (half each), the ruling is disputed; the passage explains that doubt prevents obligation.
4
Explore the rationale and the objection
The passage includes a question: why not prescribe zakat as precaution when grazing and feeding are equal? The answer is that the cause (sā'imah for most of the year) is uncertain, and obligation cannot be based on doubt.

Source Text

باب زكاة الخيل
والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في النصاب، دون العفو .
وقال محمد : تجب فيهما .
فإن قيل: إذا علفها نصف الحول، وسامت نصفه : استوى الوجوب وعدمه، فينبغي أن يترجح جانب الوجوب ؛ احتياطاً؛ لأنه عبادة، ومبناها على الاحتياط.
قيل: إنما لا تثبت الزكاة؛ لأنه وقع الشك في ثبوت سبب الإيجاب، والترجيح إنما يكون بعد ثبوت السبب.
قوله: (والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف واجبةٌ في النصاب،
دون العفو، وقال محمد وزفر : تتعلق بالنصاب والعفو). وفائدته فيما إذا هلك العفو، وبقي النصاب: يبقى كل الوجوب عندهما وقال محمد :وزفر يسقط بقدر الهالك.
كما إذا كان له تسع من الإبل، حال عليها الحول، ثم هلك منها أربع: فعليه في الباقي شاة عندهما، وقال محمد وزفر عليه في الباقي خمسة
أتساع شاة.
وكذا إذا كان معه ثمانون من الغنم حال عليها الحول، فهلك منها
أربعون : فعليه في الباقي شاة عندهما، وعند محمد وزفر: نصف شاة.
وإن هلك ستون فنصف شاة، وعند محمد وزفر: ربع شاة.
ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة : يُصرف الهلاك بعد العفو إلى النصاب الأخير، ثم الذي يليه، إلى أن ينتهي ؛ ؛ لأن الأصل هو النصاب الأول، وما زاد
عليه : تابع له.
Chapter on Zakat of Horses. And the grazing livestock (sā'imah) are those that suffice with pasture for most of their year. If he fed them half the year or more, there is no zakat on them. And this is if the price of the grazing livestock reaches a nisāb by itself; but if it does not reach a nisāb, it is added, by consensus. And as for the price of tithed food and the price of the slave who paid his fitr sadaqa, it is added, by consensus. And if he sold the livestock before the year for dirhams or for livestock, he adds the price to its kind, by consensus, i.e., he adds dirhams to dirhams, and livestock to livestock. And if he made the livestock after he had paid zakat on it fed ('alūfah), then sold it, he adds its price, by consensus; because it left the ruling of zakat wealth, so it no longer remains a nisāb. His statement: (And the sā'imah are those that suffice with pasture for most of their year). Because owners of grazing livestock may not find an alternative but to feed their livestock at some times, so the lesser is made dependent on the greater. Then this which he mentioned of grazing regarding the obligation of zakat on grazing livestock is only if the grazing is for milk and offspring; but if it is for trade, or it is valid for carrying and riding, then no zakat is due on them at all. His statement: (If he fed them half the year or more, there is no zakat on them). (1) i.e., the zakat of grazing livestock is not due on them. Chapter on Zakat of Horses. And the zakat, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, is on the nisāb, not on the excess ('afw). And Muhammad said: It is due on both. If it is said: If he fed them half the year and they grazed half the year, the obligation and its absence are equal, so the side of obligation should be preferred, as a precaution, because it is worship and its basis is precaution. It is said: Zakat is not established only because doubt occurred in the establishment of the cause of obligation, and preference is only after the establishment of the cause. His statement: (And zakat, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, is obligatory on the nisāb, not on the excess, and Muhammad and Zufar said: It attaches to the nisāb and the excess). And its benefit is when the excess perishes and the nisāb remains: the entire obligation remains according to them, and Muhammad and Zufar said it falls by the amount of the perished. Just as if he had nine camels, the year passed over them, then four of them perished: he owes on the remainder one sheep according to them, and Muhammad and Zufar said he owes on the remainder five-ninths of a sheep. Similarly, if he had eighty sheep, the year passed over them, then forty of them perished: he owes on the remainder one sheep according to them, and according to Muhammad and Zufar: half a sheep. And if sixty perished, then half a sheep, and according to Muhammad and Zufar: a quarter of a sheep. And for this reason Abu Hanifa said: Loss is allocated after the excess to the last nisāb, then to what follows it, until it ends; because the origin is the first nisāb, and what is added to it is dependent on it.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, covers two main topics: the definition and conditions for zakat on grazing livestock (sā'imah), and an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether zakat attaches to the entire herd or only to the nisāb. The commentator begins by defining sā'imah as livestock that depend on natural pasture for most of the year. If the owner feeds them for half the year or more, they are considered 'alūfah (fed) and no zakat is due because the condition of being sā'imah is not fulfilled. The reasoning is that since owners may need to feed their animals occasionally, the lesser period of feeding is treated as subsidiary to the greater period of grazing. The author then specifies that this applies only when the animals are kept for milk and breeding; if they are used for trade, transport, or riding, no zakat is due at all. The text also discusses consensus rulings on adding the sale price of sā'imah to other zakatable assets when determining the nisāb, emphasizing that after zakat is paid, if the livestock become 'alūfah and are sold, the price is added to similar assets by consensus. A question is raised: if an animal grazes for half the year and is fed for half, the factors for and against obligation are equal, so why not prescribe zakat as a precaution since worship is based on caution? The answer is that zakat is not established because the cause (being sā'imah for most of the year) is in doubt, and preference can only be given after the cause is certain. The second part presents a known intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is only obligatory on the nisāb (the minimum threshold) and not on the excess ('afw). Muhammad and Zufar, however, hold that zakat attaches to the entire herd, including the excess. The practical difference appears when some animals perish during the year. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the loss is first allocated to the 'afw, so the obligation on the nisāb remains unaffected. According to Muhammad and Zufar, the loss reduces the total herd proportionally, and the zakat obligation is reduced accordingly. Examples with camels and sheep illustrate this: with nine camels (nisāb for camels is 5, so the first 5 are nisāb and the remaining 4 are 'afw), if 4 camels die, Abu Hanifa says the loss covers the 'afw entirely, so zakat (one sheep) is still due on the remaining 5 (nisāb). Muhammad says the loss is proportional, so zakat is five-ninths of a sheep. Similarly with 80 sheep (nisāb for sheep is 40), if 40 die, Abu Hanifa says zakat (one sheep) is still due on the remaining 40, while Muhammad says half a sheep. The passage concludes by stating Abu Hanifa's principle: loss is applied first to the 'afw, then to subsequent portions of nisāb, because the first nisāb is the origin and the excess is dependent on it.

Key Terms
السائمة (as-sā'imah): Livestock that graze on natural pasture for the majority of the year, as opposed to being fed by the owner.
النصاب (an-nisāb): The minimum number or value of livestock that triggers the obligation of zakat.
العفو (al-'afw): The excess number of livestock beyond the nisāb that does not carry an additional zakat obligation according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum period of grazing that qualifies livestock as sā'imah?
A) Half the year
B) More than half the year
C) The entire year
D) Any amount of grazing

Key Takeaway
Livestock are only subject to zakat if they are sā'imah—grazing for most of the year—and are kept for milk or breeding, not trade or transport.

Zakat — Almsgiving

The Hanafi Dispute: Does Zakat Attach to the Nisāb Only or the Entire Herd?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of livestock excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar regarding zakat on the 'afw (excess), explain their proofs, and apply the ruling to calculate zakat when some livestock perish.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf limit zakat to the nisāb; the excess is immune. Muhammad and Zufar include the entire herd proportionally.

Within the Hanafi school, there is a classic dispute about whether zakat on grazing livestock covers only the minimum threshold (nisāb) or the entire herd including the excess ('afw). This lesson unpacks the arguments, the practical consequences when animals are lost, and the reasoning of each side.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: zakat is obligatory on the nisāb part only, not on the excess ('afw). Muhammad and Zufar: zakat attaches to both the nisāb and the 'afw proportionally.
2
Understand the rational argument for each side
Abu Hanifa's view: the original obligation is on the nisāb, and the excess is a follower. Muhammad's view: the entire herd is of the same species and the obligation spreads like zakat on trade goods.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The difference appears when livestock perish during the year. According to Abu Hanifa, the loss is first applied to the 'afw, so the nisāb's zakat remains intact. According to Muhammad, the loss is proportional, reducing the zakat liability.
Example: 9 camels (5 nisāb + 4 'afw). If 4 die, Abu Hanifa says zakat is still 1 sheep on the remaining 5; Muhammad says 5/9 sheep.

وهذا إذا كان ثمن السائمة يبلغ نصاباً بانفراده، أما إذا كان لا يبلغ نصاباً: ضمه، بالإجماع.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Zakat on Horses – Nassab vs 'Afw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of zakat on horses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether zakat on horses applies to the nassab only or to both nassab and 'afw, and explain the reasoning (talil) behind each.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf limit zakat to the nassab; Muhammad and Zufar extend it to the entire herd – the difference emerges when the surplus perishes.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of zakat on grazing horses (khayl sa'imah). While all Hanafi imams agree that zakat is wajib on such horses, they differ on whether it applies only to the minimum threshold (nassab) or also to the surplus ('afw). Understanding this dispute is essential for calculating zakat correctly and appreciating the subtlety of Hanafi istidlal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State precisely what Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf hold vs Muhammad & Zufar. Note that the dispute is about the scope, not the obligation itself.
All agree zakat is wajib on horses that graze (sa'imah) for the majority of the year.
2
Analyze the talil (rationale)
The text raises a question: if the horse is fed half the year and grazes half, why isn't obligation preferred as a precaution? The answer: doubt is about the cause (sabab), not about the ruling after the cause is established. Preference (tarjih) applies after the cause is certain.
This illustrates a principle: doubt in the sabab prevents obligation.
3
Examine the practical consequence (thamarah)
The difference appears when the 'afw (surplus) perishes. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the full zakat remains on the nassab. According to Muhammad and Zufar, the zakat reduces proportionally. Study the camel and sheep examples to see the calculation.
The examples use nassab numbers: for camels, zakat is a sheep per 5 camels? Actually, the text uses 9 camels and 80 sheep – standard Hanafi nassab.
4
Apply the rule of attribution of perishing
Abu Hanifa attributes the perishing first to the last nassab, then sequentially. Abu Yusuf attributes it to 'afw first, then to nassab. Muhammad and Zufar treat the whole herd as one unit. This difference explains the numerical outputs.
This step is crucial for understanding the underlying theory.

Source Text

باب زكاة الخيل
والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في النصاب، دون العفو .

قيل: إنما لا تثبت الزكاة؛ لأنه وقع الشك في ثبوت سبب الإيجاب، والترجيح إنما يكون بعد ثبوت السبب.
قوله: (والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف واجبةٌ في النصاب، دون العفو، وقال محمد وزفر : تتعلق بالنصاب والعفو). وفائدته فيما إذا هلك العفو، وبقي النصاب: يبقى كل الوجوب عندهما وقال محمد :وزفر يسقط بقدر الهالك.

وإن هلك ستون فنصف شاة، وعند محمد وزفر: ربع شاة.
ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة : يُصرف الهلاك بعد العفو إلى النصاب الأخير، ثم الذي يليه، إلى أن ينتهي ؛ لأن الأصل هو النصاب الأول، وما زاد عليه : تابع له.
وإذا هلك المالُ بعد وجوب الزكاة : سقطت .
وقال أبو يوسف : يُصرف الهلاك إلى العفو أوَّلاً ، ثم إلى النصاب شائعاً. ! بيانه أربعون من الإبل، حال عليها الحول، فهلك منها عشرون: ففي الباقي أربع شياه عند أبي حنيفة.
وقال أبو يوسف : فيها عشرون جزءاً من ستة وثلاثين جزءاً من بنت لبون.
وقال محمد وزفر: نصف بنت لبون
* قوله : (وإذا هلك المال بعد وجوب الزكاة: سقطت عنه). قيَّد بالهلاك ؛ لأن الاستهلاك لا يُسقطها ؛ لأن الزكاة تجب عليه بعد الحول، وهو يمسكها على طريق الأمانة، فإذا استهلكها: ضمنها، كالوديعة.
ثم الهلاك إنما يُسقطها : إذا كان قبل مطالبة الساعي بها، أما إذا طلبها، ولم يسلّمها إليه مع القدرة: فقد قال الكرخي: يجب عليه الضمان، وهو قول العراقيين؛ لأنها أمانةٌ طالبه بها من يملك المطالبة ، فصار كالمودع إذا طلب الوديعة، فلم يدفعها إليه مع الإمكان حتى هلكت.
وقال أبو طاهر الدباس وأبو سهل : لا يضمن.
قال في «النهاية» : وهذا أقرب إلى الفقه ؛ لأن وجوب الضمان يستدعي تفويتاً، ولم يوجد فأما في منع الوديعة فقد بدل اليد، فصار مفوتاً ليد المالك، فيضمن.
Chapter on Zakat of Horses. Zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is on the nassab, not on the 'afw. Muhammad said: It is obligatory on both. If it is said: If he feeds it half the year and it grazes half, the obligation and its absence are equal, so the side of obligation should be preferred as a precaution because it is worship and its foundation is precaution. It is said: Zakat is not established because doubt occurs in the establishment of the cause of obligation, and preference is only after the establishment of the cause. His statement: (Zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is obligatory on the nassab, not on the 'afw, and Muhammad and Zufar said: It attaches to both nassab and 'afw). Its benefit is that if the 'afw perishes and the nassab remains: the full obligation remains according to them, and Muhammad and Zufar said: it decreases by the amount of the perished. Just as if he had nine camels, a year passed, then four of them perished: on the remaining one sheep according to them, and Muhammad and Zufar said: on the remaining five-ninths of a sheep. Likewise, if he had eighty sheep, a year passed, then forty perished: on the remaining one sheep according to them, and according to Muhammad and Zufar: half a sheep. And if sixty perished: half a sheep, and according to Muhammad and Zufar: a quarter of a sheep. For this reason Abu Hanifa said: Perishing is attributed after the 'afw to the last nassab, then to the one before it, until it ends, because the origin is the first nassab, and what is added to it is subsidiary to it. And if the wealth perishes after the obligation of zakat, it is waived. Abu Yusuf said: Perishing is attributed first to the 'afw, then to the nassab in a shared manner. Its explanation: forty camels, a year passed, then twenty perished: on the remaining four sheep according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: on it twenty parts of thirty-six parts of a bint labun. Muhammad and Zufar said: half a bint labun. * His statement: (And if the wealth perishes after the obligation of zakat: it is waived for him). He specified perishing because consumption does not waive it; because zakat is obligatory upon him after the year, and he holds it as a trust, so if he consumes it, he is liable for it, like a deposit. Then perishing only waives it if it is before the demand of the tax collector. However, if he demanded it and he did not deliver it to him despite ability: al-Karkhi said: he must guarantee it, and it is the saying of the Iraqis; because it is a trust demanded by one who has the right to demand, so it becomes like the depositor when he demands the deposit and he does not give it to him despite possibility until it perishes. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and Abu Sahl said: He does not guarantee. It is said in al-Nihayah: This is closer to fiqh; because the obligation of guarantee requires a loss (tafwit), which did not occur. As for preventing the deposit, the hand has changed, so he becomes someone who has caused loss to the owner's hand, so he guarantees.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira deals with two related topics: the obligation of zakat on horses and the effect of perishing of zakatable wealth after the obligation becomes due. The author first presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether zakat on horses (sa'imah) is wajib on the entire herd or only on the nassab (the minimum number that triggers zakat). Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is wajib only on the nassab, not on the 'afw (the surplus beyond nassab). Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar hold that it is wajib on both nassab and 'afw collectively. A question is raised: if a horse is fed for half the year and grazes for half, the obligation is equalized, so precaution would suggest making it wajib; but the response is that the doubt is about the existence of the cause of obligation, and preference is applied only after the cause is established. The practical difference appears when the 'afw perishes and only the nassab remains: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the full zakat remains on the nassab; according to Muhammad and Zufar, the zakat reduces proportionally to the loss. Examples with camels and sheep are given to illustrate the calculations. Then the author discusses the ruling when zakatable wealth perishes after zakat becomes due. Generally, if the wealth perishes (halak) before payment, the zakat is waived. However, if the owner consumes it (istihlak), he remains liable because he breached the trust. A further dispute arises if the tax collector demands payment and the owner delays until the wealth perishes: al-Karkhi and the Iraqis hold that the owner must compensate, while Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and Abu Sahl hold no compensation is due. The author of al-Nihayah prefers the latter view, arguing that compensation requires a wrongful act (tafwit), which is absent when the owner merely delays but does not actively cause the loss. In contrast, in the case of a deposit (wadi'ah), the depositor's demand changes the hand of the trustee, making delay a wrongful act.

Key Terms
نصاب (nassab): The minimum number or amount of zakatable wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat. For horses, it is a specific number (e.g., five or more, depending on the type).
عفو ('afw): The surplus or excess beyond the nassab. In the context of this passage, it refers to the additional animals beyond the minimum nassab that are not subject to zakat according to some.
سائمة (sa'imah): Grazing livestock that pasture for the majority of the year. This is a condition for zakat on animals in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, on what part of a horse herd is zakat wajib?
A) On the entire herd regardless of size
B) Only on the nassab (minimum number), not on the 'afw (surplus)
C) Only on the 'afw, not on the nassab
D) On neither, as zakat on horses is not wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that zakat on horses is wajib only on the nassab, not on the surplus.

The Effect of Perishing (Halak) and Consumption (Istihlak) on Zakat Obligation
Ruling on perishing vs consumption of zakatable wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between halak (perishing) and istihlak (consumption) in zakat and state the ruling on each, and identify the dispute regarding liability after the tax collector's demand.

Core Idea
Perishing (halak) waives zakat; consumption (istihlak) does not, because the owner breached the trust.

In this lesson, we examine the consequences of zakatable wealth being destroyed after zakat becomes due. The key distinction is between involuntary perishing (halak) and voluntary consumption (istihlak). A further dispute arises when the tax collector demands payment and the wealth perishes due to delay. Understanding these rules is crucial for determining when zakat liability persists or is waived.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish halak and istihlak
Halak (perishing) is beyond the owner's control and waives zakat. Istihlak (consumption) is voluntary and the owner remains liable because he held the wealth as a trust (amanah).
The analogy is with a deposit (wadi'ah): if the deposit perishes, the depositee is not liable; if he consumes it, he is liable.
2
Apply to the case of post-obligation perishing
If the wealth perishes after zakat becomes due but before payment, zakat is waived. This is the default rule.
The text adds 'قيَّد بالهلاك' (he specified perishing) to exclude consumption.
3
Examine the dispute on delay after demand
If the tax collector demands zakat and the owner delays, then the wealth perishes: al-Karkhi and the Iraqis say the owner must compensate (like a depositor who delays returning the deposit). Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and Abu Sahl say no compensation. The author of al-Nihayah prefers the latter view because there is no active wrongdoing (tafwit).
The distinction is between preventing the deposit (which changes the hand) and merely delaying zakat (which does not).
4
Understand the rationale of al-Nihayah
Compensation requires a wrongful act (tafwit) that causes the loss. Mere delay without a change in the hand does not constitute tafwit. In the deposit case, preventing return alters the hand, which is a positive act causing loss.
This illustrates a subtle application of the principle of liability based on hand (yad).

Source Text

باب زكاة الخيل
والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف في النصاب، دون العفو .
وقال محمد : تجب فيهما .
فإن قيل: إذا علفها نصف الحول، وسامت نصفه : استوى الوجوب وعدمه، فينبغي أن يترجح جانب الوجوب ؛ احتياطاً؛ لأنه عبادة، ومبناها على الاحتياط.
قيل: إنما لا تثبت الزكاة؛ لأنه وقع الشك في ثبوت سبب الإيجاب، والترجيح إنما يكون بعد ثبوت السبب.
قوله: (والزكاة عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف واجبةٌ في النصاب، دون العفو، وقال محمد وزفر : تتعلق بالنصاب والعفو). وفائدته فيما إذا هلك العفو، وبقي النصاب: يبقى كل الوجوب عندهما وقال محمد :وزفر يسقط بقدر الهالك.
كما إذا كان له تسع من الإبل، حال عليها الحول، ثم هلك منها أربع: فعليه في الباقي شاة عندهما، وقال محمد وزفر عليه في الباقي خمسة أتساع شاة.
وكذا إذا كان معه ثمانون من الغنم حال عليها الحول، فهلك منها أربعون : فعليه في الباقي شاة عندهما، وعند محمد وزفر: نصف شاة.
وإن هلك ستون فنصف شاة، وعند محمد وزفر: ربع شاة.
ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة : يُصرف الهلاك بعد العفو إلى النصاب الأخير، ثم الذي يليه، إلى أن ينتهي ؛ لأن الأصل هو النصاب الأول، وما زاد عليه : تابع له.
وإذا هلك المالُ بعد وجوب الزكاة : سقطت .
وقال أبو يوسف : يُصرف الهلاك إلى العفو أوَّلاً ، ثم إلى النصاب شائعاً. ! بيانه أربعون من الإبل، حال عليها الحول، فهلك منها عشرون: ففي الباقي أربع شياه عند أبي حنيفة.
وقال أبو يوسف : فيها عشرون جزءاً من ستة وثلاثين جزءاً من بنت لبون.
وقال محمد وزفر: نصف بنت لبون

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira deals with two related topics: the obligation of zakat on horses and the effect of perishing of zakatable wealth after the obligation becomes due. The author first presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether zakat on horses (sa'imah) is wajib on the entire herd or only on the nassab (the minimum number that triggers zakat). Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar hold that it is wajib on both nassab and 'afw collectively. A question is raised: if a horse is fed for half the year and grazes for half, the obligation is equalized, so precaution would suggest making it wajib; but the response is that the doubt is about the existence of the cause of obligation, and preference is applied only after the cause is established. Key Terms
هلاك (halak): The perishing or destruction of zakatable wealth without the owner's fault. This can waive the zakat obligation if it occurs before payment.
استهلاك (istihlak): Consumption or use of the zakatable wealth by the owner. This does not waive zakat because the owner is considered to have breached the trust and thus remains liable.
تفويت (tafwit): An act of causing loss actively. In the context, it is the required condition for liability according to the preferred view.

Key Takeaway
Perishing (halak) waives zakat, but consumption (istihlak) does not; after demand, there is a dispute on liability.

Destruction of Zakatable Wealth: Halaak vs. Istihlak and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling on halaak of wealth after zakat becomes due, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between halaak (destruction) and istihlak (consumption) in zakat, apply the Hanafi position that halaak drops the obligation while istihlak does not, and calculate zakat after partial destruction according to the three Hanafi imams.

Core Idea
Destruction after zakat is due drops the obligation; consumption does not — the owner holds wealth as a trust.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi zakat law: when wealth perishes without fault, the obligation is lifted, but if the owner consumes it, liability remains. The text also presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on calculating zakat when only part of the nisab is destroyed, and another on whether refusing the collector's demand creates liability. Understanding these nuances is essential for accurate fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule and its condition
The matn states: if wealth perishes (halaak) after zakat becomes wajib, the obligation drops. The key condition is that it is genuine destruction, not consumption (istihlak). The owner holds the wealth as a trust (amanah), so only fault (consumption) makes him liable.
The analogy to deposit (wadi'ah) is central.
2
Examine the ikhtilaf on partial destruction
Using the example of 40 camels, 20 destroyed: Abu Hanifa treats the remaining 20 as a new nisab (4 sheep). Abu Yusuf attributes the loss proportionally to the surplus and nisab (20/36 of a bint labun). Muhammad and Zufar attribute the loss entirely to the nisab (1/2 bint labun).
The thamarah (practical difference) in zakat amount is significant.
3
Analyze the second ikhtilaf on liability after demand
If the collector demands zakat and the owner refuses to hand over the specific asset, then the asset is destroyed: The Iraqis (al-Karkhi) equate this to a depositor who refuses to return the deposit, making the owner liable. The Transoxiana scholars (Abu Tahir al-Dabbas, Abu Sahl) argue that since the owner may give the value, he is not obliged to deliver the specific asset, so no liability arises.
The key point is the owner's option (takhyir) between asset and value.
4
Identify the tarjih and mufta bihi
Al-Nihaya and the majority of Transoxiana scholars prefer the view of no liability after demand. For partial destruction, Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah).
The mufta bihi: no liability upon refusal, and calculation per Abu Hanifa.
5
Evaluate the overall dispute
Both disputes revolve around the analogy to deposit (amanah). The owner is a trustee; destruction without fault is excusable, but consumption is a breach. The option to give value reinforces the trustee's limited liability.
The school's consistency in applying the trust analogy is evident.

Source Text

باب زكاة الخيل
وإذا هلك المالُ بعد وجوب الزكاة : سقطت .
وقال أبو يوسف : يُصرف الهلاك إلى العفو أوَّلاً، ثم إلى النصاب شائعاً. بيانه أربعون من الإبل، حال عليها الحول، فهلك منها عشرون: ففي الباقي أربع شياه عند أبي حنيفة.
وقال أبو يوسف : فيها عشرون جزءاً من ستة وثلاثين جزءاً من بنت لبون.
وقال محمد وزفر: نصف بنت لبون
* قوله : (وإذا هلك المال بعد وجوب الزكاة: سقطت عنه). قيَّد بالهلاك ؛ لأن الاستهلاك لا يُسقطها ؛ لأن الزكاة تجب عليه بعد الحول، وهو يمسكها على طريق الأمانة، فإذا استهلكها: ضمنها، كالوديعة.
ثم الهلاك إنما يُسقطها : إذا كان قبل مطالبة الساعي بها، أما إذا طلبها، ولم يسلّمها إليه مع القدرة: فقد قال الكرخي: يجب عليه الضمان، وهو قول العراقيين؛ لأنها أمانةٌ طالبه بها من يملك المطالبة ، فصار كالمودع إذا طلب الوديعة، فلم يدفعها إليه مع الإمكان حتى هلكت.

وفي البدائع (۱) : كافة مشايخ ما وراء النهر قالوا: لا يضمن ولو طلب الساعي؛ لأن المالك مخيَّر: إن شاء أعطاه العين أو قيمتها، فلم يلزمه تسليم العين، فصار كما قبل المطالبة.
قال في «النهاية»: والأصح عدم الضمان.
(۱) بدائع الصنائع ٢٢/٢.
Chapter of Zakat of Horses. If wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory, it is dropped. Abu Yusuf said: Destruction is first attributed to the exempt portion, then to the nisab proportionally. Explanation: forty camels, one year passes, twenty are destroyed: in the remaining (twenty) there are four sheep according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: in it there are twenty parts of thirty-six parts of a bint labun. Muhammad and Zufar said: half a bint labun. His statement: (If wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory, it is dropped from him). He restricted it to destruction because consumption does not drop it; because zakat becomes obligatory upon him after the year, and he holds it in trust, so if he consumes it, he becomes liable for it, like a deposit. Then destruction only drops it if before the demand of the collector. But if he demands it and he does not hand it over while able: al-Karkhi said: liability is incumbent, and it is the saying of the Iraqis; because it is a trust demanded by one who has the right of demand, so he becomes like the depositor when he demands the deposit and he does not return it while able until it is destroyed. Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and Abu Sahl said: no liability. In al-Nihaya: This is closer to fiqh; because liability requires causing loss, and it does not exist. However, in preventing the deposit, the hand has changed, so he becomes a cause of loss of the owner's hand, so he is liable. In al-Bada'i: all the scholars of Transoxiana said: no liability even if the collector demands, because the owner has a choice: if he wishes he gives the asset or its value, so he is not obliged to deliver the asset, so it is as before the demand. In al-Nihaya: the correct view is no liability. (1) Bada'i al-Sana'i 22/2.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar deals with the ruling when zakatable wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes wajib. The main ruling (matn) states that if the wealth perishes (halaak), the obligation drops. The commentator explains that this is specific to destruction (halaak) as opposed to consumption (istihlak) because consumption constitutes a breach of trust, making the owner liable like a depositor who uses the deposit. Then he discusses the condition of the collector's demand. If the collector demands the zakat and the owner fails to hand it over despite ability, there is a difference: al-Karkhi and the Iraqis hold him liable, analogizing to a depositor who refuses to return the deposit. But Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and Abu Sahl say no liability because the owner has a choice to give the asset or its value, so he wasn't obliged to give the specific asset. The author of al-Nihaya prefers the latter as more sound, and al-Bada'i confirms that the scholars of Transoxiana agree with no liability. This lesson also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how to calculate remaining zakat when partial destruction occurs: Abu Hanifa considers the remaining nisab independently (four sheep on twenty from forty), Abu Yusuf attributes the loss proportionally to the excess and nisab (twenty parts of thirty-six of a bint labun), while Muhammad and Zufar consider the loss entirely from the nisab (half a bint labun). The mufta bihi position is that destruction drops the obligation if before demand, and no liability is incurred.

Key Terms
هلاك (halāk): Destruction of property without fault of owner, e.g., natural disaster.
استهلاك (istihlāk): Using or consuming the property, thereby breaching the trust (amanah) and incurring liability for zakat.
مطالبة الساعي (muṭālabat al-sāʿī): The demand made by the official zakat collector (sāʿī) for the owner to hand over the zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (mufta bihi), if the zakat collector demands the zakat and the owner refuses to hand over the specific asset but then the asset is destroyed before payment, what is the ruling?
A) The owner is liable and must pay zakat because he refused the collector.
B) The owner is not liable because he had the option to give the value instead of the asset.
C) The owner must pay only if the destruction was due to his negligence.
D) The owner is liable only if he consumed the asset.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between destruction (halaak) and consumption (istihlak) in zakat; destruction after wujub drops the obligation, while consumption incurs liability, and the mufta bihi view is that refusing the collector's demand does not create liability due to the owner's option to pay value.

Advancing Zakat Payment Before the Year Completes
Ruling with proof on advance zakat payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid advance zakat payment and explain the consequence if the nisab diminishes at year-end.

Core Idea
Paying zakat early is valid only if the nisab lasts until year-end; otherwise it becomes voluntary charity.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a practical question: can you pay your zakat before the year is over? The matn rules that it is valid if you own the nisab, but the commentary introduces a critical condition: the nisab must remain intact until the end of the haw. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in zakat fulfillment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and its proof
The matn says advance payment is valid (ja'iz) when the person owns nisab at the time of payment. The proof given is that the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) already exists—possession of nisab and the passing of part of the year.
The proof is rational (dalil 'aqli): obligation can be fulfilled once its cause exists.
2
Distinguish advance payment from on-time payment
The commentary from al-Nihaya highlights a key difference: for advance payment, the nisab must persist until the end of the year; for payment at the end, the nisab may diminish due to payment itself.
This is a subtle but important legal distinction (tafrīq).
3
Apply the condition to an example
If someone advances a sheep for forty camels, but at the end of the year only thirty-nine remain, no zakat is due. The payment becomes voluntary charity (sadaqah tatawwu') or the sheep can be reclaimed if still in the imam's hands.
4
Note the additional condition from al-Khujandi
Al-Khujandi states that for valid advance payment, the year must have already commenced (ḥawl munʿaqid) at the time of advancing. This is the first of three conditions he mentions.
The other two conditions are not given in this excerpt but are covered in other texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن قدَّم الزكاة على الحول، وهو مالك للنصاب: جاز)؛ لأنه أدى بعد سبب الوجوب.
آخر
قال في «النهاية»: لكن بين الأداء معجلاً، والأداء في الحول فرق، وهو أن المعجل : يُشترط فيه أن لا ينتقص النصاب في آخر الحول، وفي الأداء في آخر الحول: لا يُشترط.
بيانه: إذا عجل شاة عن أربعين فحال عليها الحول، وعنده تسع وثلاثون فلا زكاة عليه ، حتى إنه إذا كان صَرَفها إلى الفقراء : وقعت تطوعاً.
وإن كانت قائمةً بعينها في يد الإمام، أو الساعي: استردها.
وأما إذا كان أداؤه في آخر الحول وقعت عن الزكاة وإن انتقص النصاب بأدائه.
- قال الخُجندي : إنما يجوز التعجيل بشرائط ثلاث:
أحدها: أن يكون الحول منعقداً وقت التعجيل.
His statement: (If he advances zakat before the year, while he owns the nisab, it is valid); because he performed it after the cause of obligation. End. He said in al-Nihaya: But between performance in advance and performance at the end of the year there is a difference: the advanced one requires that the nisab not diminish at the end of the year, while performance at the end of the year does not have that condition. Its explanation: If he advances a sheep for forty (camels) and the year passes while he has thirty-nine, then no zakat is due; even if he had distributed it to the poor, it counts as voluntary charity. And if it still exists in the hands of the imam or the collector, he takes it back. But if his performance is at the end of the year, it counts for zakat even if the nisab diminishes by his payment. Al-Khujandi said: Advancing is only valid with three conditions: One of them: that the year has commenced at the time of advancing.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses the ruling on paying zakat before the completion of the year (ta'jil). The matn states that it is valid if the person owns the nisab at the time of advance payment. The proof given is that the cause of obligation (sabab al-wujub) — i.e., possession of nisab and passage of part of the year — has occurred. However, the commentator from al-Nihaya clarifies a crucial distinction: for advanced payment, there is a condition that the nisab must remain intact until the end of the year; otherwise, the payment is not counted as zakat but as voluntary charity. In contrast, payment made at the end of the year counts as zakat even if the act of payment reduces the nisab below the threshold. An example: if someone advances a sheep for forty camels, but at the end of the year only thirty-nine remain, no zakat is due. If the sheep was already given to the poor, it becomes sadaqah tatawwu' (voluntary). If the sheep is still in the hands of the imam or collector, the owner may take it back. Al-Khujandi adds three conditions for valid advance payment: (1) the year must have already commenced at the time of advancing (so the cause of obligation has started). The other two conditions are not mentioned in this excerpt.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (taʿjīl al-zakāt): Paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year (hawl).
انعقاد الحول (inʿiqād al-ḥawal): The commencement of the zakat year, i.e., having the intention and possession of nisab at the start.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The advance payment becomes voluntary charity (sadaqah tatawwu) and if the asset remains with the imam, the owner may take it back.
C) The owner must make up the zakat by paying again after the year.
D) The advance payment is invalid and the owner must repent.

Key Takeaway
Advance zakat payment is valid only if the nisab remains at year-end; otherwise it becomes voluntary charity.

Advancing Zakat: Conditions and Proof
States the permissibility of advancing zakat with its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid advancement (ta'jīl) of zakat according to the Hanafi school and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Advancing zakat is valid only if the year has started and the nisab remains complete at year's end.

The Hanafi school permits paying zakat before the lunar year is complete, provided certain conditions are met. This lesson examines the ruling, the evidence from qiyas, and the three conditions articulated by al-Khujandi. Understanding these conditions is essential to avoid rendering the payment voluntary charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on advancing (ta'jīl) zakat before the completion of the year. The ruling is that it is permissible (jā'iz) if conditions are met.
2
Recognize the proof (dalil)
The text provides a qiyās argument: payment is valid because it occurs after the cause of obligation (sabab) has begun. Identify the cause and how the analogy works.
3
List the three conditions from al-Khujandi
The passage explicitly lists three conditions: (1) the year has started, (2) the nisab is complete at the end of the year, (3) the principal of the nisab does not perish. Note each with its example.
4
Apply the conditions to a new scenario
Given a hypothetical change in wealth during the year, determine whether the advancement counts as zakat or falls as voluntary charity.
5
Contrast early vs. on-time payment
Al-Nihaya highlights a key difference: early payment requires year-end completeness, while on-time payment does not. Understand the practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الخيل
وإن قدم الزكاة على الحول، وهو مالك للنصاب : جاز .
وفي البدائع (۱) : كافة مشايخ ما وراء النهر قالوا: لا يضمن ولو طلب الساعي؛ لأن المالك مخيَّر: إن شاء أعطاه العين أو قيمتها، فلم يلزمه تسليم العين، فصار كما قبل المطالبة.
قال في «النهاية»: والأصح عدم الضمان.
قوله: (فإن قدَّم الزكاة على الحول، وهو مالك للنصاب: جاز)؛ لأنه أدى بعد سبب الوجوب.
آخر
قال في «النهاية»: لكن بين الأداء معجلاً، الأداء وبين في الحول فرق، وهو أن المعجل : يُشترط فيه أن لا ينتقص النصاب في آخر الحول، وفي الأداء في آخر الحول: لا يُشترط.
بيانه: إذا عجل شاة عن أربعين فحال عليها الحول، وعنده تسع وثلاثون فلا زكاة عليه ، حتى إنه إذا كان صَرَفها إلى الفقراء : وقعت تطوعاً.
وإن كانت قائمةً بعينها في يد الإمام، أو الساعي: استردها.

مثاله : إذا كان له أقل من مائتي درهم، أو أربع من الإبل، فهذا مال لا ينعقد عليه الحول، فإذا عجل الزكاةَ، ثم كَمل النصاب بعد التعجيل: لا يكون ما عجل زكاة، ويكون تطوعاً.
وكذا إذا كان له مائتا درهم فتصدق بخمسة على فقير بنية الزكاة، وانتقص النصاب بمقدار ما عجل، ولم يستفد شيئاً حتى حال الحول، والنصاب ناقص : كان ما عجل تطوعاً.
وإن استفاد شيئاً حتى كمل به النصاب قبل الحول، ثم حال الحول، والنصاب كامل: صح التعجيل عن الزكاة.
وأما إذا كان استفاد ما يكمل به النصاب بعد الحول، ثم حال الحول الثاني، ووجبت الزكاة: فما عجل لا ينوب عنها؛ لأن التعجيل حصل للحول الأول، ولم تجب عليه زكاة الحول الأول.
Chapter on zakat of horses.
And if he advances zakat before the year, while he owns the nisab, it is permissible.
In al-Bada’i‘: All the mashayikh of Transoxiana said: He is not liable even if the collector demands, because the owner has a choice: if he wishes, he gives the same animal or its value, so the delivery of the specific animal is not incumbent, so it becomes as before the demand.
Al-Nihaya says: The most correct is no liability.
His statement: (For if he advances zakat before the year, while he owns the nisab: permissible); because he performed after the cause of obligation.
Then
Al-Nihaya says: However, there is a difference between advancing early and paying at the end of the year, namely that for early payment it is conditioned that the nisab does not decrease at the end of the year, while for payment at the end of the year it is not conditioned.
Its clarification: If he advances a sheep for forty (sheep), then the year passes while he has thirty-nine, then no zakat is due; even if he had disbursed it to the poor, it falls as voluntary charity.
And if it remains in the hand of the imam or collector, he takes it back.
But if his payment was at the end of the year, it counts as zakat even if the nisab decreased by his payment.
Al-Khujandi said: Advancing is permissible only with three conditions:
First: That the year has started at the time of advancing.
Second: That the nisab for which he advanced remains complete at the end of the year.
Third: That its principal does not perish in between.
Its example: If he has less than two hundred dirhams, or four camels, then this is wealth that does not have a year started; so if he advances zakat, then the nisab becomes complete after the advancement, then what he advanced is not zakat and is voluntary.
Similarly, if he has two hundred dirhams and gives five dirhams to a poor person with the intention of zakat, and the nisab decreases by the amount he advanced, and he does not acquire anything until the year passes while the nisab is deficient, then what he advanced is voluntary.
But if he acquired something to complete the nisab before the year, then the year passes while the nisab is complete, then the advancement is valid as zakat.
As for if he acquired what completes the nisab after the year, then the second year passes and zakat becomes due, then what he advanced does not replace it, because the advancement was for the first year, and zakat was not due for the first year.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on advancing (ta‘jīl) zakat before the end of the lunar year. It opens by stating the basic ruling: if the owner owns the nisab (minimum wealth threshold) at the time of advancement, it is valid. The text then cites various authorities. From al-Bada’i‘, we learn that the leading scholars of Transoxiana hold that if the owner advances zakat, he is not held liable for any decrease in value, even if the zakat collector demands a specific animal, because the owner has the option to give either the animal or its value; thus the specific animal is not owed. Al-Nihaya affirms this as the soundest view. The author then comments on the matn, explaining that advancement is valid because it occurs after the cause of obligation (i.e., the passage of time with nisab). Next, al-Nihaya distinguishes between early payment and payment at the end of the year: early payment requires that the nisab be complete at the year’s end, whereas end-of-year payment is valid even if the nisab decreases. Examples clarify: if someone advances a sheep for forty sheep, but at year-end has only thirty-nine, the advancement becomes voluntary unless the specific sheep is recovered. Al-Khujandi then formalizes three conditions for valid advancement: (1) the year must have commenced at the time of advancing (i.e., the nisab was held for some time), (2) the nisab must still be complete at the end of the year, and (3) the principal (aṣl) of the nisab must not perish in between. The text provides several examples illustrating these conditions: insufficient initial nisab, decrease due to the advancement itself, and cases where the nisab is completed later. If the nisab is completed after the first year, the advancement does not count for the second year because it was intended for the first, which was not due.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jīl): payment of zakat before the end of the lunar year
نصاب (nisāb): minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory
حول (ḥawl): the passage of a full lunar year from the moment the nisab was first possessed

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khujandi, what is the first condition for valid advancement (ta'jīl) of zakat?
A) The nisab must be complete at the end of the year.
B) The year must have started (ḥawl mun‘aqid) at the time of advancing.
C) The principal of the nisab must not perish.
D) The zakat must be given directly to the poor.

Key Takeaway
Advancing zakat is valid only when the year has begun and the nisab remains intact until the year's end.
