Advancing Zakat for Multiple Nisabs: The Dispute with Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of ta‘jīl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on advancing zakat for multiple nisabs and apply the majority Hanafi ruling to a concrete case.

Core Idea
One nisab now can cover many future ones: intention counts over possession.

The matn declares that advancing (ta‘jīl) zakat for multiple nisabs is permissible even if you currently own only one nisab. Imam Zufar, a strict qiyas follower, objects. This lesson unpacks the disagreement, the example given, and why the majority view is the fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the mainstream Hanafi position
Identify what the text says as 'indana' (with us): it is permissible to advance for many nisabs.
2
Identify Zufar's opposing view
Zufar limits ta‘jīl to the nisab actually in possession at the time of advancement.
3
Follow Zufar's proof (qiyas)
Zufar analogizes advancement to payment before a debt is due: you cannot prepay a non‑existent obligation. The existing nisab is the only certain liability.
His logic is strict but narrow.
4
Analyse the majority response
The Hanafi majority holds that the sabab (cause) of zakat is the potential to reach nisab, which already exists with one nisab. Intention can cover future nisabs.
The text does not detail the response, but the ruling is clear.
5
Determine the thamarah al‑khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: if one nisab (5 camels) and later 20 more, the majority says no extra zakat; Zufar requires zakat for the 20. The relied upon view is the majority (indana).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز التعجيل لنُصب كثيرة إذا كان في ملكه نصاب واحد.
وقال زفر : لا يجوز إلا عن النصاب الموجود في ملكه.
حتى إنه إذا كان معه خمس من الإبل، فعجل أربع شياه، ثم تم ملكه عشرون من الإبل : فعندنا يجوز عن الكل، وعنده: لا يجوز إلا عن الخمس.
And it is permissible to advance for multiple nisabs if he owns one nisab. Zufar said: It is not permissible except for the nisab existing in his possession. For example, if he has five camels, and he advances four sheep, then he acquires twenty camels: according to us it is permissible for all, but according to him it is not permissible except for the five.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of ta‘jīl (advancing zakat). The matn states that it is permissible to advance zakat for many nisabs (i.e., for future years) even if the person currently owns only one nisab. Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a prominent Hanafi scholar known for strict adherence to qiyas, disagrees. He argues that advancement can only be for the nisab that is actually in one's possession at the time of advancing; one cannot intend to cover future nisabs that are not yet owned. The text provides a concrete example: a person owns five camels and advances four sheep (the zakat for five camels is one sheep? Actually for 5-9 camels the zakat is one sheep, but here he advances four sheep, perhaps corresponding to future nisabs). Later he acquires twenty more camels. According to the mainstream Hanafi position (our view, 'indana), the advancement covers all the camels (i.e., the original five plus the twenty), so he does not need to give additional zakat for that year. According to Zufar, the advancement only covers the original five, so he will owe zakat for the twenty. The reliance on the mainstream view is indicated by 'indana (with us), which is the operative position for fatwa.

Key Terms
نصب كثيرة (nuṣub kathīrah): multiple nisabs, meaning multiple thresholds of zakat wealth (e.g., for different years or categories)
زفر (Zufar): Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a major Hanafi scholar who often used strict qiyas
تعجيل (ta‘jīl): advancing payment of zakat before the end of the year/obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does 'indana' indicate regarding the two positions?
A) Zufar's view is the strongest.
B) The majority view is the one relied upon.
C) Both views are equally valid for fatwa.
D) The dispute is unresolved.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority allows advancing zakat for multiple future nisabs, while Zufar restricts it to the currently owned nisab; the operative fatwa follows the majority.

Advancing Zakat (Ta'jil): Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Ushr Timing
Intra-madhhab dispute on advancing tithe and general rules of ta'jil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for advancing zakat (ta'jil) and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding advancing 'ushr before vegetation.

Core Idea
Advancing zakat is valid if the cause exists, but for 'ushr, Abu Yusuf permits after cultivation; Muhammad demands vegetation, and his view is preferred.

The permissibility of paying zakat before its obligation becomes due depends on whether the cause (sabab) is established. For livestock, advancing is generally allowed if the nisab exists. For crops, the dispute between the two great disciples of Abu Hanifa—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad—revolves around the exact moment when the obligation becomes certain. This lesson examines their disagreement and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios of ta'jil
The passage discusses two main cases: (1) advancing zakat payment to a poor person before the year ends, and (2) advancing 'ushr on crops at various stages.
The first case illustrates the general principle; the second is the focus of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Extract the general rule for payment to a poor person
If one pays zakat early to a poor person and later the payer becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes, the payment remains valid. The key is that at the time of payment, the recipient was poor.
3
Analyze the three timings for 'ushr
The text distinguishes: (a) before cultivation → invalid, (b) after cultivation and after vegetation → valid, (c) after cultivation but before vegetation → disputed.
Vegetation here means the plants have visibly appeared.
4
State the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf permits advancing 'ushr after cultivation even before vegetation; Muhammad does not. The text declares Muhammad's view as al-azhar (the more apparent).
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
A farmer who pays 'ushr after cultivation but before vegetation would have to repeat the payment if he follows the preferred view, but not if he follows Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة الخيل
-
قال: لأن كل نصاب أصل بنفسه.
ولنا: أن النصاب الأول هو الأصل فى السببية، والزوائد عليه تابعة له. ولو عجل أداء الزكاة إلى فقير، ثم أيسر قبل الحول، أو مات، أو ارتد: جاز ما دفعه عن الزكاة ؛ لأن الدفع صادف الفقر، فما يحدث بعده من الغنى والموت: لا يؤثر فيه.
ولو عجل شاةً عن خمس من الإبل، فهلكت جميعها وله أربعون
من الغنم: لا تقع الشاة عنها. كذا في الينابيع».
وأما تعجيل العشر : إن كان قبل الزراعة : لا يجوز، وإن كان بعد
الزراعة وبعد النبات: جاز.
فإن كان بعد الزراعة قبل النبات: جاز عند أبي يوسف.
وعند محمد : لا يجوز، وهو الأظهر.
- وإن عجل عُشر ثمر النخيل : إن كان بعد طلوعها: جاز، وإن كان
قبله : لا يجوز.
Chapter of Zakat on Horses. He said: Because every nisab is an origin by itself. But we argue: The first nisab is the origin in causing (obligation), and additions to it are subordinate to it. If one advances payment of zakat to a poor person, and then (the payer) becomes wealthy before the end of the year, or dies, or apostatizes: what he paid is valid for the zakat; because the payment met poverty, and what occurs afterwards of wealth or death does not affect it. If one advances a sheep for five camels, and then all the camels perish while he owns forty sheep: the sheep does not count for them (the camels). As is it in al-Yanabi'. As for advancing the tithe ('ushr): if it is before cultivation: not permissible; if it is after cultivation and after vegetation: permissible. If it is after cultivation but before vegetation: permissible according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: not permissible, and it is the more apparent. And if one advances the tithe of date palms: if after their appearance (the dates): permissible; if before it: not permissible.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on advancing zakat (ta'jil) before the end of the year. The text begins with an objection from an unnamed source (likely a non-Hanafi scholar) that each nisab is an independent cause of obligation. The Hanafi response (ولنا) is that the first nisab is the original cause, and any additional wealth is subordinate to it. The ruling: if one pays zakat early to a poor person, and then the payer becomes rich, dies, or apostatizes before the year ends, the payment is still valid because it met the condition of poverty at the time of payment. However, if one pays a sheep from a nisab of camels (five camels) and then the camels perish, and the person now owns forty sheep (a separate nisab), the sheep paid does not count for the camels because the nisab of camels is gone. As for advancing the tithe on crops (ushr): it is not permitted before cultivation, but it is permitted after cultivation and after the plants appear. A dispute arises between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: Abu Yusuf allows advancing after cultivation but before plants appear; Muhammad disallows it. The author says Muhammad's view is الأظهر (more apparent). Similarly, advancing tithe on dates is allowed only after the dates appear, not before.

Key Terms
التعجيل (al-ta'jīl): The act of paying zakat before its obligation becomes due (before the end of the year or harvest).
العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe (10%) on agricultural produce due as zakat.
النصاب (al-niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone advances a sheep for five camels, then all camels perish and he now owns forty sheep, what is the ruling?
A) The sheep does not count for the camels.
B) The sheep counts for the camels because the nisab was present at payment.
C) The sheep counts for the forty sheep instead.
D) He must pay another sheep for the forty sheep.

Key Takeaway
Advancing zakat is valid only if the cause of obligation exists at the time of payment; for 'ushr before vegetation, the preferred Hanafi view does not allow it.

Zakat on Silver: Nisab and Included Assets
Definition of nisab for silver and its implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab of silver for zakat and identify which forms of silver are included in the calculation.

Core Idea
Zakat on silver is due on 200 dirhams (each 14 qirats) and includes all silver assets—cash, jewelry, utensils—aggregated together.

This passage lays out the foundational rule for zakat on silver in the Hanafi school. It establishes the minimum threshold (nisab) and clarifies that all forms of silver, not just coins, are subject to zakat when combined. Understanding this definition is essential for correctly calculating one's zakat obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab threshold
Locate the explicit statement that no zakat is due on less than 200 dirhams. Note that the dirham is defined by weight (14 qirats each).
The nisab is fixed; it does not vary with market value.
2
Understand the dirham definition
Each dirham in the nisab is specified to weigh 14 qirats. This is a classical measure; in modern terms, it is approximately 2.975 grams, but the exact weight is historically defined.
The same weight applies to the zakat payment (5 dirhams).
3
Recognize the scope of silver assets
The text says 'silver includes minted and unminted, and wariq (silver coins)'. Also, the term 'riqah' is specific to minted coins. Then a long list follows: dirhams, rings, sword mounts, etc.
Zakat is not limited to cash; jewelry, utensils, and ornaments are also included.
4
Apply the aggregation rule
All silver items in one's ownership are combined to determine if the total reaches the nisab. Partial ownership or mixed assets are aggregated.
This prevents evasion by dividing wealth into small non-zakatable portions.
5
Note the practical implication
A person must calculate the total weight of all silver they own (coins, jewelry, decorative items) at the end of the lunar year. If it equals or exceeds 200 dirhams weight, 2.5% is due.
Gold has its own separate nisab and is treated independently.

Chapter of Zakat on Silver. Charity (zakat) is not due on less than two hundred dirhams. When it reaches two hundred dirhams and one year passes, then five dirhams are due. Chapter of Zakat on Silver. He gave precedence to silver over gold because it is more commonly circulated among people; do you not see that the dower (mahr), the nisab for theft, and the values of damaged goods are estimated by it. Then silver encompasses minted and unminted, and wariq (silver coins). And al-riqah is specific to minted coins; its plural is riqūq with a dammah on the ra. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (There is no charity on less than two hundred dirhams, when it is two hundred dirhams) i.e., weighed, the weight of each dirham being fourteen qirats, (and one year passes over it, then five dirhams are due, the weight of each dirham being fourteen qirats). Upon this are built the rulings of zakat, the nisab for theft, the assessment of blood money (diyat), dower, and land tax (kharaj). Whether the silver is minted, unminted, or jewelry, all that he owns is collected together, including dirhams, rings, sword mounts, bridles, saddles, stars in the Qur'an, vessels, and nails fixed in knives.

Commentary
This passage defines the nisab for zakat on silver. The author states that no zakat is due on less than 200 dirhams. The dirham is defined as weighing 14 qirats (specific weight; in classical Hanafi fiqh, this is about 2.975 grams each, but the exact weight is defined historically). When one possesses 200 dirhams and a lunar year passes, 5 dirhams (i.e., 2.5%) are due. The author notes that silver is given precedence over gold in the chapter because it is more commonly used in transactions; many legal values (mahr, nisab of theft, diyat, etc.) are based on silver. The term 'silver' (فضة) includes both minted coins (مضروب) and unminted silver (غير مضروب) as well as the collective term 'ورق'. The term 'رقّة' specifically refers to minted silver coins. The nisab and zakat apply to all forms of silver wealth: coins, jewelry, utensils, etc. All items of silver in one's ownership are aggregated to determine if the total reaches the nisab. The list given includes dirhams, rings, sword decorations, bridles, saddles, stars (ornaments in Qur'an), vessels, nails, etc. This comprehensive list shows that zakat is not limited to cash but extends to all silver assets.

Key Terms
فضة (fiḍḍah): Silver, including both minted coin (مضروب) and unminted silver (غير مضروب), and the term 'ورق' refers to silver coins.
رقّة (riqqah): Specifically minted silver coins; plural رقوق.
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of silver (200 dirhams weight of 14 qirats each) that triggers zakat.

Zakat on silver is wajib when you own 200 dirhams weight (14 qirats each) for one lunar year, and you must include all silver items—coins, jewelry, utensils—in the calculation.

Zakat on Silver: Nisab of 200 Dirhams and Standard Weight
Establishes nisab and due amount for silver zakat with historical proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab and due amount for silver zakat according to the Hanafi school and explain the historical basis for the 14-qirat dirham weight.

Core Idea
Zakat on silver is due on 200 dirhams (14 qirats each) at 2.5%, based on the standard established by Caliph Umar.

The passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar establishes the core ruling for silver zakat: the nisab is 200 dirhams, and the due amount is 5 dirhams. But it also provides a fascinating historical account of how the dirham weight came to be fixed at 14 qirats. This lesson will guide you through the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence that makes this standard authoritative in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level? The passage discusses the obligation of zakat on silver.
Zakat on silver is fard ayn when conditions are met.
2
State the nisab and due amount
What is the minimum quantity (nisab) and what must be paid? The passage states: 200 dirhams, each of 14 qirats, and the due is 5 dirhams.
This is 2.5% of the nisab.
3
Identify the conditions for obligation
What conditions must be present for zakat to become due? The passage mentions: nisab, passage of one lunar year (hawl), and complete ownership.
Other conditions like free growth are implicit.
4
Examine the historical proof for the dirham weight
Why is the dirham set at 14 qirats? The passage narrates that during the Prophet's time, dirhams had varying weights (20, 10, 12 qirats). Caliph Umar, to facilitate taxation, had accountants derive a median weight of 14 qirats.
This historical practice is considered a proof (dalil) for the standard.
5
Apply the ruling to mixed silver items
How do we combine different forms of silver? The passage states that all silver items—coins, jewelry, vessels—are combined by weight to reach the nisab. Value due to craftsmanship does not count.
This is a distinctive Hanafi ruling.

Chapter on Zakat of Silver. Charity: There is nothing on less than two hundred dirhams. So when there are two hundred dirhams and a year has passed over them, then five dirhams are due on them. He gave precedence to it over gold because it is more commonly circulated among people; do you not see that the dowry, the nisab of theft, and the values of damaged goods are estimated by it. Then silver includes minted and unminted, and al-wariq (silver). And al-riqqah is specific to minted coins; its plural is ruqūq with damm on the rā. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (There is no charity on less than two hundred dirhams; so when there are two hundred dirhams): that is, weighed, the weight of each dirham being fourteen qirats; (and a year has passed over them: then five dirhams are due on them, each dirham weighing fourteen qirats. Upon this are based the rulings of zakat, the nisab of theft, the estimation of blood money, the dowry, and the land tax. Whether the silver is minted, unminted, or jewelry, all that one owns of it, including dirhams, rings, sword fittings, bridles, saddles, stars in the Quran, vessels, nails set in knives, bracelets, armlets, anklets, and other such things, are combined. If the total weight reaches two hundred dirhams, then five dirhams are due on it; otherwise no. And the year does not commence for it until it reaches two hundred. If its weight is less than two hundred but its value due to quality and craftsmanship equals two hundred, nothing is due on it. The origin of this is that the weights during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) varied. Among them was the weight of the dirham of twenty qirats, called the weight of ten; among them was its weight of ten qirats, called the weight of five; and among them was twelve qirats, called the weight of six. They would exchange among themselves until the time of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). He wanted to collect the land tax from them, so he demanded the higher weight, which was difficult for them. They asked him for leniency, so he gathered the accountants of his time to mediate between them. They derived for him the weight of seven. They took three dirhams weighing forty-two qirats, divided them into thirds, so each dirham became fourteen qirats. And that is because the weight of seven equals ten mithqals; because if you take ten dirhams from each type, the total becomes twenty-one mithqals. If you take one third of that, it becomes seven mithqals. Its illustration is that you multiply each one by ten and sum them: it becomes four hundred twenty mithqals. Then you divide it by twenty: the result of the division is one...
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on zakat of silver, with historical proof for the standard dirham weight. The author begins by stating the core ruling: no zakat is due on less than 200 dirhams. When one possesses 200 dirhams (each weighing 14 qirats) and a full lunar year passes, the due amount is 5 dirhams (2.5%). This matches the nisab and rate in the Hanafi school. The commentator explains why silver is mentioned before gold: it is more commonly used in transactions, such as dowries, theft nisab, and compensation values. The term 'silver' includes both minted (coins) and unminted forms, as well as jewelry. The commentator then emphasizes that all silver items one owns—including coins, rings, sword fittings, bridles, saddles, stars inscribed in Qurans, vessels, nails in knives, bracelets, armlets, anklets, etc.—are combined to reach the nisab. The year only begins once the total weight reaches 200 dirhams. If the silver is below that weight but its value due to craftsmanship equals 200 dirhams, no zakat is due because zakat is based on weight, not value. The passage provides a fascinating historical background for the standard dirham weight of 14 qirats, attributed to Caliph Umar. During the Prophet's time, dirhams had various weights (20, 10, and 12 qirats). To simplify taxation, Umar convened accountants who derived a middle weight: they took three dirhams of different weights totaling 42 qirats, divided by three, giving 14 qirats per dirham. This standard became fixed for all calculations of zakat, theft nisab, blood money, etc. The commentator also gives a mathematical demonstration showing that seven ten-dirham lots of different weights sum to 21 mithqals, and one-third is 7 mithqals, corresponding to 10 dirhams of 14 qirats each. This establishes the authoritative weight for the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
فضة (fiddah): Silver, including minted coins, unminted metal, and jewelry.
درهم (dirham): Unit of weight and currency; each Hanafi dirham weighs 14 qirats (approximately 3.36 grams).
نصاب (nisab): The minimum quantity of wealth required for zakat to become obligatory; for silver, 200 dirhams.
رقة (riqqah): Minted silver coins; plural ruqūq.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1/20 of a mithqal; here 1 dirham = 14 qirats.
حول (hawl): The passage of one lunar year after possession of the nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 100 dirhams of 14 qirats each

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school fixes the silver nisab at 200 dirhams of 14 qirats each, with zakat of 5 dirhams (2.5%).

Zakat on Silver: Weight Standards and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Excess Amounts
Explains weight standard and intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat for excess silver.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standardized dirham weight (14 qirats) established by Caliph Umar and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on calculating zakat for silver amounts exceeding 200 dirhams.

Core Idea
Zakat on silver is by weight, not value; Abu Hanifa requires increments of 40 dirhams above 200, while the Sahibayn apply a proportional rate.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah explains the historical background of dirham weights in early Islam and the standardization under Caliph Umar. It also presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the calculation of zakat on silver amounts that exceed the nisab of 200 dirhams. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi rulings on zakat in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on nisab for silver
Note that zakat becomes wajib only when the weight of silver reaches 200 dirhams. If the weight is less but the value equals 200, no zakat is due. This establishes that the basis is weight, not value.
This is a condition (shart) for zakat on silver.
2
Trace the historical weight standardization
The passage describes three different dirham weights used during the Prophet's time. Umar gathered his accountants and derived an average weight of 14 qirats per dirham (the 'weight of seven'). Understand the mathematical derivation: three dirhams weighing 42 qirats divided by 3 gives 14 qirats.
This standardization is the basis for the Hanafi nisab.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position on the increase (ziyadah)
Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on the excess amount until it reaches 40 dirhams. Then 1 dirham is due alongside the original 5 dirhams (for 200), and for every additional 40 dirhams, 1 dirham. This avoids fractional dirhams.
This is based on the principle that fractions are not considered for zakat increments.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that any amount above 200 dirhams is subject to proportional zakat at the rate of 1/40. So for 230 dirhams, zakat is 5.75 dirhams (5 + 30/40).
They rely on the general analogy (qiyas) that the rate remains constant.
5
Compare the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the actual amount of zakat due. For example, 230 dirhams: Abu Hanifa says 5 dirhams, Sahibayn say 5.75 dirhams. For 240 dirhams: both say 6 dirhams (same at exactly 240). Note where they coincide.
The conflict arises only when the excess is not a multiple of 40.

ولا ينعقد عليها الحول حتى تبلغ مائتين، فإن كان وزنها دون المائتين، وقيمتها لجودتها وصياغتها تساوي مائتين: فلا شيء فيها. وأصل هذا أن الأوزان كانت على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مختلفة، فمنها ما كان زنة الدرهم عشرين قيراطاً، وهو الذي يسمى وزن عشرة ومنها ما كان وزنه عشرة قراريط، وهو الذي يسمى: وزن خمسة، ومنها ما كان اثني عشر قيراطاً، وهو الذي يسمى: وزن ستة. فكانوا يتصارفون بها إلى زمان عمر رضي الله عنه، فأراد أن يستوفي منهم الخراج فطالبهم بالأكثر، فشق عليهم، فالتمسوا منه التخفيف، فجمع حُساب زمانه ليتوسطوا بينهم، فاستخرجوا له وزن السبعة، فجمعوا ثلاثة دراهم وزنها اثنان وأربعون قيراطاً، فقسموها أثلاثاً، فكان كل درهم: أربعة عشر قيراطاً. وإنما كانت السبعة وزن عشرة مثاقيل ؛ لأنك إذا جمعت من كل صنف عشرة دراهم : صار الكل إحدى وعشرين مثقالاً، فإذا أخذت ثلث ذلك : كان سبعة مثاقيل. وصورته أنك تضرب كل واحد منها في عشرة، وتجمعه: يكون أربعمائة وعشرين مثقالاً، ثم تقسمها على عشرين : يصح من القسمة : أحد وعشرون، فثلثه سبعة. واعلم أنك متى زدت على الدرهم ثلاثة أسباعه صار مثقالاً؛ لأن المثقال عشرون قيراطاً، ومتى نقصت من المثقال ثلاثة أعشاره وهي ستة : كان درهماً؛ لأن الدرهم أربعة عشر قيراطاً. قوله: (ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعين درهماً، فيكون فيها درهم مع الخمسة، ثم في كل أربعين درهماً درهم عند أبي حنيفة). قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: ما زاد على المائتين: فزكاته بحسابه)، قلت الزيادة أو كثرت حتى لو كانت الزيادة درهماً : ففيه جزء من أربعين جزءاً من درهم، وهو ربع عشره. قوله: (وإذا كان الغالب على الوَرِق: الفضة: فهي في حكم الفضة)؛ لأنها إذا كانت هي الغالبة : كان الغش مستهلكاً، فلا اعتبار به.
And the year (hawl) does not begin for it until it reaches two hundred (dirhams). If its weight is less than two hundred, but its value due to quality and craftsmanship equals two hundred, then nothing is due. The origin of this is that weights were different in the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). Among them was that the dirham weighed twenty qirats, which is called the weight of ten; and among them was what weighed ten qirats, which is called the weight of five; and among them was what weighed twelve qirats, which is called the weight of six. They used to exchange them until the time of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). He wanted to collect the kharaj from them, so he demanded the greatest (weight), which was difficult for them. They sought leniency from him, so he gathered the accountants of his time to mediate between them. They extracted for him the weight of seven, so they collected three dirhams weighing forty-two qirats, divided them into thirds, so each dirham was fourteen qirats. It was only that seven was the weight of ten mithqals because if you collect from each type ten dirhams, the total becomes twenty-one mithqals, and if you take one third of that, it is seven mithqals. Its form is that you multiply each one by ten and add them up: it becomes four hundred and twenty mithqals, then divide by twenty: the result of division is twenty-one, so its third is seven. Know that if you add to the dirham three-sevenths of it, it becomes a mithqal because the mithqal is twenty qirats; and if you subtract from the mithqal three-tenths of it, which is six, it becomes a dirham because the dirham is fourteen qirats. His saying: (And nothing is due on the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then there is in it one dirham along with the five, then for every forty dirhams one dirham according to Abu Hanifa). His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Whatever exceeds two hundred, its zakat is by its calculation), I say: whether the increase is small or large, even if the increase is one dirham, then in it is a fraction of one-fortieth of a dirham, which is one-tenth of its quarter. His saying: (And if the majority of the silver coins (wariq) is silver, then it is in the ruling of silver) because if it is the majority, the adulteration is considered perished, so no consideration is given to it.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage discusses the zakat on silver, specifically the weight standards for dirhams and a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on how to calculate zakat for amounts exceeding 200 dirhams. The commentator begins by explaining that for silver items, the annual zakat cycle only begins when the weight reaches 200 dirhams. If the weight is less but the value equals 200 due to craftsmanship, no zakat is due because the basis is weight, not value. He then provides historical background on the different dirham weights in early Islam: the 'weight of ten' (20 qirat), 'weight of five' (10 qirat), and 'weight of six' (12 qirat). People used these until the caliphate of Umar, who standardized the dirham at 14 qirat (the 'weight of seven') by averaging the three types. This is derived from taking three dirhams (sum of their weights = 42 qirat) and dividing into three equal parts (14 qirat each). The commentator explains the mathematical relationship: adding 3/7 of a dirham gives a mithqal (20 qirat), and subtracting 3/10 of a mithqal (6 qirat) gives a dirham (14 qirat). Next, the passage addresses the ruling on 'increase' (ziyadah) above 200 dirhams. Abu Hanifa holds that no zakat is due on the increase until it reaches 40 dirhams, at which point 1 dirham is due, and then for every additional 40 dirhams, 1 dirham. For example, if one has 230 dirhams, the zakat is 5 dirhams (on 200) plus nothing for the 30 because it's less than 40. If one has 240, then zakat is 6 dirhams (5 + 1). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that any amount above 200 is subject to proportional zakat at the rate of 1/40, so for 230 dirhams, zakat is 5.75 dirhams. The text does not explicitly prefer one view, but the weight standard of 14 qirat is considered the relied-upon (mu'tamad) among the later scholars. Finally, the passage rules that if the majority of a mixed metal item is silver, it is treated as silver for zakat purposes because the impurity is considered negligible.

Key Terms
الدرهم (al-dirham): A standard silver coin; in this context, the canonical dirham weighs 14 qirats (according to Umar's standardization).
القيراط (al-qirat): A unit of weight; in this text, the standard dirham is 14 qirats and the mithqal is 20 qirats.
المثقال (al-mithqal): A unit of weight equal to 20 qirats; used as a reference for gold nisab.
الوَرِق (al-wariq): Silver coins or silver ingots; in this context, it refers to silver money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the weight of the standard dirham established by Caliph Umar?
A) 20 qirats
B) 14 qirats
C) 10 qirats
D) 12 qirats

Key Takeaway
Zakat on silver is based on weight (200 dirhams of 14 qirat each), and for excess amounts, Abu Hanifa requires full 40-dirham increments while the Sahibayn apply proportional zakat.

Zakat on Silver: The Nisab and Rate (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat calculation for silver

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab and rate of zakat on silver according to the Hanafi school, and explain the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding zakat on amounts exceeding 200 dirhams.

Core Idea
For silver, zakat is 1 dirham per 40; but beyond 200 dirhams, the Sahibayn apply proportional calculation while Abu Hanifa applies a per-40 block.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute on how to calculate zakat on silver when the amount exceeds 200 dirhams. While the basic rate is 1 dirham for every 40, the two disciples differ from Imam Abu Hanifa on how the excess over 200 is treated. Understanding this thamarah al-khilaf is essential for correct zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base nisab and the rule for excess
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams. The text states: 'nothing in the increase until it reaches 40 dirhams, then in it is one dirham.' This means that after the nisab, zakat is due on complete blocks of 40 dirhams.
The base nisab of 200 dirhams is assumed from earlier sections.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that for every complete 40 dirhams above the nisab, 1 dirham zakat is due. Any excess less than 40 dirhams is not zakatable.
This is the literal reading of the text: 'in every 40 dirhams, one dirham.'
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that any amount exceeding 200 dirhams is subject to zakat at the rate of 1/40, regardless of whether the excess constitutes a complete 40.
They apply the proportional rate (bil-hisab) to the entire excess.
4
Apply both positions to a concrete example
Consider 230 dirhams total. Abu Hanifa: zakat on 200 dirhams = 5 dirhams, no zakat on the 30 dirhams excess (since less than 40), total 5 dirhams. Sahibayn: zakat on entire 230 at 1/40 = 5.75 dirhams.
The difference is 0.75 dirhams.
5
Conclude with thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that small increments above the nisab may escape zakat under Abu Hanifa's view, while the Sahibayn's view always taxes them proportionally.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, but the Sahibayn's view is also recognized.

Source Text

باب زكاة الفضة
ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعين درهماً، فيكون فيها درهم.
ثم في كل أربعين درهماً : درهم عند أبي حنيفة .
وقالا : ما زاد على المائتين : فزكاته بحسابها .
وعشرون مثقالاً: فثلثه سبعة.
وقال محمد بن الفضل : المعتبر في كل زمان بدرهمه، وبه أفتى جماعة من المتأخرين ، إلا أن الأول هو المعتبر، وهو أربعة عشر قيراطاً،
وعليه إطباق كتب المتقدمين والمتأخرين، وهو الأظهر. واعلم أنك متى زدت على الدرهم ثلاثة أسباعه، مثقالاً؛ لأن المثقال عشرون قيراطاً، ومتى نقصت من المثقال ثلاثة أعشاره وهي ستة : كان درهماً؛ لأن الدرهم أربعة عشر قيراطاً. قوله: (ولا شيء في الزيادة حتى تبلغ أربعين درهماً، فيكون فيها درهم مع الخمسة، ثم في كل أربعين درهماً درهم عند أبي حنيفة). * قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: ما زاد على المائتين: فزكاته بحسابه)، قلت الزيادة أو كثرت حتى لو كانت الزيادة درهماً : ففيه جزء من أربعين جزءاً من درهم، وهو ربع عشره.
Chapter of Zakat of Silver. And there is nothing in the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then in it is one dirham. Then in every forty dirhams: one dirham according to Abu Hanifa. And they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: What exceeds two hundred, its zakat is in proportion to it. And twenty mithqals: its third is seven. And Muhammad ibn al-Fadl said: The standard in every time is its dirham, and a group of later scholars gave fatwa accordingly, except that the first is the standard, which is fourteen qirats, and upon it is the agreement of the books of the earlier and later scholars, and it is the most apparent. And know that whenever you add to the dirham three sevenths of it, it becomes a mithqal; because the mithqal is twenty qirats, and whenever you subtract from the mithqal three tenths of it, which are six, it becomes a dirham; because the dirham is fourteen qirats. His saying: (And there is nothing in the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then in it is one dirham with the five, then in every forty dirhams one dirham according to Abu Hanifa). * His saying: (And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: What exceeds two hundred, its zakat is in proportion to it), I say: whether the increase is small or large, even if the increase were one dirham, then in it is a part of forty parts of a dirham, which is one fortieth (literally a quarter of its tenth).
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on zakat of silver. The matn states that no zakat is due on silver until it reaches 40 dirhams (nisab), then 1 dirham is due. For every additional 40 dirhams, 1 dirham is due according to Imam Abu Hanifa. However, the two disciples (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) hold that for amounts exceeding 200 dirhams, the zakat is calculated proportionally (i.e., 1/40 of the excess). This is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute. The passage then discusses the weight of the dirham relative to the mithqal (gold coin). The standard dirham is 14 qirats, while the mithqal is 20 qirats. Thus, 7 dirhams equal 5 mithqals (since 7*14=98, 5*20=100, approximate), and the text shows the conversion: adding 3/7 of a dirham gives a mithqal. The preferred weight standard is 14 qirats per dirham. The commentary also reiterates the nisab and the dispute.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin of a specific weight, here standardized at 14 qirats.
مثقال (mithqal): A gold coin of 20 qirats weight.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1 qirat = 1/20 of a mithqal or 1/14 of a dirham.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the zakat on 210 dirhams of silver?
A) 5 dirhams
B) 5.25 dirhams
C) 1 dirham
D) No zakat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether small excesses above the silver nisab are subject to zakat, with Abu Hanifa's block system prevailing as mufta bihi.
